### H.H.Vy (@hoanghvy)
_Fri Jun 19 16:40:27 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/hoanghvy/status/2068011036406591694)

> I was watching a Bloomberg video on YouTube about space-based data centers, and a lightbulb suddenly went off in my head: Could Sivers Semiconductors $SIVE lasers actually benefit from this trend?
>
> Here is my attempt to map out the thesis and connect the dots.
>
> 1/ How do you even build a data center in space?
> It sounds like sci-fi, but it’s becoming the next major frontier as Elon Musk has openly discussed it with Starlink, and a startup called StarCloud has already launched the first GPU-equipped satellite into orbit. They’ve even successfully run an Nvidia H100 in space to train an LLM for the very first time.
>
> The core idea is to bypass Earth's strained power grids entirely. By putting data centers directly into orbit, you get uninterrupted, 24/7 solar energy without weather or night-cycle disruptions. Instead of massive air conditioning units, these satellites dump heat using specialized radiators into the vacuum of space.
>
> However, a single satellite is essentially just one GPU rack. To function like a true, high-performance AI data center, you can't have isolated chips floating in silos. You need entire swarms of these satellites linked together in real time, functioning as one giant, distributed supercomputer cluster.
>
> 2/ Why lasers are the only viable solution
> To make these orbital clusters work, you need massive bandwidth on a strict power budget. Lasers are the only technology that checks both boxes.
>
> Think of data transfer like a water hose: the width of the hose determines how much water (data) you can move, and that width is dictated by the frequency of the wave you use.
>
> Radio Waves (The Old Way): Traditional satellites use radio frequencies. It’s a low-frequency, wide beam that is easy to aim, but it's the equivalent of a garden hose. It's perfectly fine for simple commands or beam-down TV signals, but it completely chokes on the terabits-per-second traffic that a GPU cluster generates internally. Plus, to get anywhere near the required bandwidth with radio, you’d need massive, heavy antennas—and every extra kilogram launched into space costs a fortune.
>
> Lasers / Optical (The New Way): Light operates at a vastly higher frequency, meaning the "hose" is massive. You can cram an incredible amount of data through a laser beam. It’s the exact same reason our home internet upgraded from copper wires to fiber optics.
>
> In space, power is everything because you are limited to what your solar panels and batteries can generate. Lasers are incredibly efficient, delivering vastly more data per watt than radio. While the engineering challenge is steep, you have to precisely aim a laser pointer across thousands of km of vacuum, the payoff is undeniable. Radio will always have a place for low-stakes backup communications because it's reliable, but for the heavy-duty data shifting an AI cluster demands, lasers are the only option that fits both the bandwidth and the weight budget.
>
> 3/ Where does Sivers $SIVE fit into this?
> This is where the investment thesis gets interesting. Sivers explicitly lists SATCOM (Satellite Communications) as one of its core target markets, right alongside terrestrial AI data centers. It’s the exact same underlying laser and photonics platform, just packaged for orbital links instead of ground-based server racks.
>
> To be clear: I haven’t found any official announcements, contracts, or partnerships linking Sivers to Starcloud, Crusoe, or any specific space-data-center project yet.
>
> But here is the thesis: If these satellite swarms scale up the way Musk, Bezos, and major tech investors are betting they will, someone has to supply the advanced photonics hardware. Sivers is one of only a handful of companies with proven, high-power DFB (Distributed Feedback) laser technology sitting right at the intersection of AI optics and satellite communication.
>
> There's no signed contract on paper today, but given how fast this market is moving, it’s absolutely a name to keep on your radar.
> $SIVE

> The AI buildout has moved through two major bottlenecks:
>
> Power and Memory (HBM).
>
> The next structural constraint is already forming,  interconnects and data movement at massive scale.
>
> Copper is hitting its physical limits on bandwidth, reach, and power. The industry’s answer is silicon photonics + Co-Packaged Optics (CPO). $LITE $AAOI $NVDA 
>

### Zeek | Insights 📊 (@ZeekTyt)
_Fri Jun 19 16:56:18 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/ZeekTyt/status/2068015026485469360)

> 2/
> Why this layer matters now:
>
> As AI clusters grow to tens of thousands of GPUs, the amount of data that needs to move between chips explodes. When accelerators sit idle waiting for data, the economics break.
>
> Silicon photonics moves data with light instead of electricity. It delivers higher bandwidth density, lower power per bit, and longer reach than copper.
> The shift from traditional pluggable optics to CPO is accelerating in 2026.

---

### Zeek | Insights 📊 (@ZeekTyt)
_Fri Jun 19 16:56:19 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/ZeekTyt/status/2068015028595208263)

> 3/
> The silicon photonics supply chain (AI data center focus):
>
> Upstream
> •  SOI wafers (base substrate)
> •  Indium Phosphide (InP) — the critical material for high-performance lasers. No scalable substitute exists today.
>
> Lasers & Active Components
> •  InP-based EMLs and continuous-wave lasers
> •  Key names: $LITE (Lumentum) and $COHR (Coherent)
>
> Design & Fabrication
> •  Photonic Integrated Circuits (PICs)
> •  $TSM (TSMC) COUPE platform is currently leading for AI-relevant integration
>
> Advanced Packaging & CPO
> •  This is becoming the new bottleneck layer
> •  TSMC CoWoS + COUPE stacking for co-packaged optics
>
> Downstream
> •  High-speed transceivers (800G/1.6T+)
> •  Optical switches and fabrics (NVIDIA, Broadcom, Marvell) $NVDA $MRVL $AVGO

---

### Zeek | Insights 📊 (@ZeekTyt)
_Fri Jun 19 16:56:20 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/ZeekTyt/status/2068015035222249783)

> 5/
> $TSM COUPE is emerging as the central integration platform.
> •  65nm silicon photonics base already in volume production
> •  COUPE (Compact Universal Photonic Engine) uses advanced stacking to combine electrical and photonic dies
> •  Targeted for meaningful CPO volume in 2026
> •  $NVDA is already shipping early TSMC-backed CPO switches
>
> As CPO moves from pluggables into co-packaged and deeper integration, TSMC’s packaging capacity becomes a key gating factor.

### Semi Doped (@semidoped)
_Fri Jun 19 18:35:33 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 23 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/semidoped/status/2068040004220395798)

> Tower, Marvell pass five million coherent photonic ICs
>
> Tower Semiconductor (NASDAQ/TASE: TSEM) and Marvell Technology have shipped more than five million coherent photonic integrated circuits built on Tower's silicon photonics platform, the Israeli foundry said Thursday from Migdal Haemek. The chips are used in coherent optical modules for data center interconnects, where they support higher bandwidth and lower power per bit than legacy approaches. Tower manufactures the photonic ICs at its fabs and supplies them to Marvell, which integrates them into its coherent digital signal processor-based optical products. Neither company disclosed the value of the shipments or named end customers. (Tower Semiconductor)
>
> Vik:
> This announcement is only one thing: a flex to show who is building more SiPho chips right now. Googled "GF shipments SiPho" and came up with 3 substacks (one was mine). Flex is working.
>
> @austinsemis @vikramskr

### Finn Stockinger (@FinnStockinger)
_Fri Jun 19 19:49:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 180 · ↻ 27 · 💬 15 · [open on X](https://x.com/FinnStockinger/status/2068058639626293756)

> Why did I even get interested in $IQE?
>
> When the entire market went absolutely crazy over $AXTI - I was swallowing the bitter pill of being late to that specific party.
>
> But since I hate losing, I immediately started asking myself: what is next?
>
> I always try to look one step ahead. 
>
> That is exactly how I managed to get early into names like $IQE or $LPKF and others before the masses caught on.
>
> But back to $IQE - why this specific company?
>
> The global frenzy and massive demand for optical lasers are just getting started.
>
> The market quickly realized that Indium Phosphide (InP) - the core substrate material - does not just fall from the sky. 
>
> Hence, the massive explosive run on $AXTI.
>
> But a raw InP wafer by itself is practically useless for high-performance photonics.
>
> You have to actually do something with it before it can become a functioning laser.
>
> Epitaxy.
>
> Epitaxy is the atomic-scale deposition of crystal layers onto that substrate.
>
> Only a handful of companies globally possess the highly specialized MOCVD and MBE machinery required for this advanced process.
>
> One company listed on the London Stock Exchange  owns a significantly larger fleet of these reactors than almost anyone else, giving them a massive structural scale advantage.
>
> Say hello to $IQE.
>
> Look at the pure-play competition for epi-wafers. Landmark Optoelectronics possesses far fewer machines, yet because it sits on a different exchange (Taiwan), it historically traded at multiples that make IQE look like an absolute deep-value steal.
>
> And if you want proof of their technological moat: 
>
> IQE was just confirmed as the second largest patent filer in the entire UK for semiconductor devices. 
>
> This isn't a speculative small-cap; it’s an IP powerhouse.
>
> Now, to be completely fair, IQE had a dark cloud hanging over it.
>
> The cyclical semiconductor downturn cut their 2025 revenue to £97m, and because chip fabs have massive fixed costs, underutilization completely crushed their near-term margins.
>
> Worse, geopolitical tensions flared as China introduced strict export controls on critical raw materials like Gallium and Antimony.
>
> If you check most standard financial screeners today, that ugly debt and supply-chain risk warning still pop up.
>
> But the market is looking backward.
>
> First, IQE completely neutralized the China risk by successfully recycling 100% of their Gallium Arsenide and Indium Phosphide wafer waste directly back into ultra-pure raw materials for their production lines.
>
> Second, on May 28, 2026 - the ultimate balance sheet reset happened.
>
> IQE officially completed a transformational £81 million strategic recapitalization package.
>
> MACOM Technology Solutions ($MTSI) stepped up to anchor the deal - injecting £30m in direct equity and £15m in new convertible notes to secure a ~15% strategic stake. 
>
> Existing institutional notes were swapped into equity, and the old HSBC bank debt was entirely wiped out.
>
> The balance sheet is clean. The financial risk is gone.
>
> So, who is MACOM and why does this partnership matter?
>
> MACOM is a heavyweight in high-performance semiconductor products for Data Centers, Aerospace, and Defense. 
>
> They design the brains - the optical components and ICs that power next-generation networks.
>
> By deeply aligning with IQE, MACOM secures a stable Western supply chain for advanced epi-wafers. 
>
> For IQE, it guarantees immediate structural volume demand to fill those empty reactors and unlock massive operating leverage.
>
> And the momentum shift is already visible.
>
> Photonics has officially overtaken wireless to become IQE’s largest segment (58.7% of revenue), propelled by surging AI data center demand and immediate US military and defense funding releases.
>
> Think that is all? 
>
> We got another massive confirmation of their turnaround strategy.
>
> IQE followed this up by solidifying their multi-year agreement with Tower Semiconductor ($TSEM).
>
> Together, they are scaling Silicon Photonics (SiPh) via the heterogeneous integration of IQE’s advanced epitaxy layers directly onto Tower’s silicon wafers. 
>
> This allows them to build optical transceivers that handle the insane data transfer speeds required by modern AI architectures.
>
> The pieces of the puzzle are coming together perfectly.
>
> The market is still pricing $IQE like a distressed, underutilized UK small-cap because backward-looking financial data feeds haven't adjusted to the new post-deal reality.
>
> They are missing the bigger picture.
>
> The debt is gone, the largest players in the chip space are anchoring equity deals to secure capacity, and IQE sits right at the choke point of the entire optical computing revolution.
>
> While the crowd is still chasing raw substrates, the smart money is moving to the epitaxy bottleneck.
>
> Now you understand why $IQE?

### BULL OF BRITAIN (@BULLOFBRITAIN)
_Fri Jun 19 20:02:41 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 105 · ↻ 16 · 💬 7 · [open on X](https://x.com/BULLOFBRITAIN/status/2068061930741227839)

> Round 2 of high sentiment AI trades with retard explanations at the end.

> In my opinion these are the greatest companies in their respective sectors, I genuienly don't think you could find better. Sectors covered - Cloud servicing, Memory, CPO, NPO, Copper, Testing, Transmitters, Switches (NFA)
>
> $NBIS - pure play AI cloud infrastructure, renting out GPU compute at scale, backed by NVDA.
> (you rent their computers to run AI instead of buying your own)
>
> $SNDK (or any other memory play) - NAND flash and SSD maker, riding the AI storage demand wave.
> (the chips that store all the data the AI models need to remember)
>
> $MRVL - custom AI silicon and optical/electrical interconnect for hyperscaler data centers.
> (the chips that move data between the AI chips, and the custom brains the big clouds order)
>
> $AEHR - test and burnin systems for AI chips and silicon photonics, screening parts before they ship.
> (the machines that stress-test chips so the broken ones get caught before they go in a server)
>
> $AAOI - vertically integrated optical transceivers, makes the lasers and optics for data center networking in-house.
> (the parts that turn data into light to fire it across the data center)
>
> $IQE - epitaxial wafer supplier, grows the compound semiconductor layers that photonics and RF chips are built on.
> (the raw special wafers everyone else builds their laser and signal chips on top of)
>
> $SMTC - high speed signal integrity platform for 800G, 1.6T and 3.2T transmitters.
> (the chips that move faster data inside AI clusters)
>
> $CRDO - active electrical cables and SerDes connectivity, making copper carry AI data faster over short reaches.
> (the smart cables that let cheap copper move data fast enough for AI racks)

### Gaetano (@crux_capital_)
_Fri Jun 19 20:06:31 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 113 · ↻ 6 · 💬 15 · [open on X](https://x.com/crux_capital_/status/2068062894105952499)

> Some thoughts on $AXTI…
>
> As I work through the China AI optics supply ramp, the AXT setup keeps getting more complicated.
>
> China is reportedly preparing a ~$295B five-year AI data-center buildout plan.
>
> At the same time, the domestic optics stack is ramping everywhere:
>
> > Source Photonics / Dongshan is expanding optical chips and modules.
>
> > Chinese suppliers are pushing EMLs, CW lasers, InP PICs, silicon photonics and optical engines.
>
> > Yunnan Germanium, Guangdong Xiandao and AXT / Tongmei are expanding InP substrate output.
>
> > Innolight and Eoptolink continue scaling data-center transceivers.
>
> So on one hand, this is clearly positive for AXT’s China-based demand. Domestic China demand is cleaner because the export-permit issue really shows up when substrates leave China.
>
> If China’s AI buildout absorbs more domestic optical supply, AXT could be sitting in the middle of a very important local bottleneck.
>
> But there is another side.
>
> More domestic InP substrate capacity from Yunnan Germanium, Guangdong Xiandao and others could reduce AXT’s pricing power over time if those suppliers scale and qualify.
>
> And the geopolitical angle cuts both ways.
>
> China has real leverage here. If it wanted to slow U.S. substrate availability, it does not need to fully ban exports. It can continue to slow permits, condition approvals, request more end-user data, or prioritize domestic demand.
>
> That would be supportive for China’s own AI optics ecosystem, but it would also make AXT look less like a globally fungible supplier and more like a China-centered strategic substrate asset. That deserves a much different multiple. 
>
> At the same time, China has limits.
>
> They still want Innolight, Eoptolink, Source and others selling into global hyperscalers.
>
> They also still need parts of the global tool stack, especially for high-end InP photonics. China is localizing MOCVD and test where it can, but the most proven high-end InP tool ecosystem still appears heavily tied to companies like $aixa and $veco
>
> So the AXT debate is really evolving. 
>
> InP demand up
> China AI buildout up
> Domestic substrate competition up
> Export-permit risk up
> Geopolitical chokepoint value up
>
> That combination can be very bullish, but it also changes the type of business the market is underwriting.
>
> Anyway, just thinking out loud here as I work through this report and come to stronger conclusions. Treat this as a brain dump rather than what my final assumption will be .
>
> Open to dialogue!

---

### Arnaud Mercier - #Entrepreneur #Versailles (@arnaudmercier)
_Fri Jun 19 20:08:40 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/arnaudmercier/status/2068063435644907871)

> <p>Q1 2026 was a bumper quarter in venture capital. Investors deployed $300 billion of fresh capital, more than double the previous quarter and surpassing 70% of all venture spending in 2025.</p>
>
> <p>The devil is, of course, in the detail: $188 billion of that cash went to four companies &#8211; OpenAI, Anthropic, xAI, and Waymo &#8211; accounting for 60% of all venture capital deployed in Q1.</p>
>
> <p>VCs generally revel in change, but even by our standards what it takes to raise has shifted at an unprecedented rate over the past 12 months: expectations of early-stage founders &#8211; in terms of defensibility, scaling,&nbsp;and pricing &#8211; have been completely rewritten.</p>
>
> <p>Fearing the ‘AI-pocalypse’, early-stage founders could be forgiven for feeling despondent seeing these figures. The outlook looks daunting, but it doesn’t need to be. The concentration of capital around a handful of AI giants is changing the rules, but the game goes on. The question for founders right now is not whether Big AI wins, but how can smaller companies survive and thrive alongside it.</p>
>
> <h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>A Rising Tide Is Lifting&nbsp;<em>Most</em>&nbsp;Boats</strong></h2>
>
> <p>Investment in the US rose 190% YoY in Q1 but deal count fell 26%, meaning that capital is concentrating into fewer, larger cheques. However, the remaining $112 billion of funding sits in line with recent quarterly highs, and the environment for smaller rounds remains robust.</p>
>
> <p>Frontier lab mega-rounds do not directly compete with early-stage cheques: indeed, pre-Seed to Series A companies are growing faster than ever before. <a href="https://t.co/bpppVubFcZ" target="_blank">Stripe</a> recently revealed data showing that the top 100 AI-native companies are scaling from $1 million to $30 million ARR five times faster than previous software generations.</p>
>
> <p>It’s still a very good time to be an early-stage AI company, especially one that can move quickly and provide genuine agentic solutions rather than simple GPT wrappers. That distinction matters because the startups most under threat are those with no meaningful moat &#8211; i.e. businesses that lack sufficient brand, switching costs or economies of scale. These companies will be squeezed not only by platform owners from above them, but also by falling prices below them.</p>
>
> <h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Learnings from the SaaSpocalypse</strong></h2>
>
> <p>It wasn&#8217;t so long ago that Anthropic&#8217;s Claude Cowork launched and within hours wiped hundreds of millions off the valuations of some of the world&#8217;s leading software companies. Investors and founders alike feared that a new army of AI agents was about to eat everybody&#8217;s lunch.</p>
>
> <p>As of June 2026, however, debate on the death of SaaS is ongoing. Enterprise customers could theoretically vibe code much of their own software, but very few are actually going to do so. At least not yet. At the same time, the opposing view &#8211; that concerns about model companies are entirely overblown &#8211; has become equally unhelpful. The phrase &#8220;what if model companies do this?&#8221; has become a catch-all objection that often substitutes for harder conversations around business fundamentals.</p>
>
> <p>The right question is not whether model companies will kill software. They won&#8217;t. It’s which software companies will become stronger as models improve, and which will become increasingly commoditised by them. That distinction matters because the bar to raise has doubled while investor attention has narrowed dramatically. Raising money outside AI is a tough ask in 2026, but that doesn’t mean every company needs to become an AI company. It means founders need to ask harder questions.</p>
>
> <p>If OpenAI or Anthropic launched this feature tomorrow, what would still belong to us? Are we building a product, or are we building an advantage? Do we control proprietary data, hardware, scientific know-how, distribution, or regulation? Does our business become stronger as models improve, or weaker? Would customers still choose us if intelligence itself became abundant and cheap? These are the questions investors are asking too.</p>
>
> <h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>The Best Offense Is a Good Defense</strong></h2>
>
> <p>Whatever you do as an early-stage founder right now, defense is key.</p>
>
> <p>Investors are gravitating towards sectors like robotics, defence, photonics, biotech, and novel compute. This isn’t because they are fashionable, but because they possess characteristics that are difficult for foundation model providers to replicate.</p>
>
> <p>Robotics and defence require integration with the physical world, complex systems, and long customer relationships. Photonics and novel compute rely on years of scientific research and manufacturing expertise. Biotech combines proprietary data, regulatory barriers, and deep domain knowledge. Intelligence alone is not enough.&nbsp;</p>
>
> <p>Investors are looking for companies with assets that cannot simply be replaced by agents. Proprietary data, specialised hardware, scientific expertise and difficult-to-reproduce infrastructure are becoming durable moats.&nbsp;</p>
>
> <p>No matter what, we are in for a turbulent remainder of 2026. Capital is concentrating at every level, the revenue bar to raise has roughly doubled in five years, and the companies getting funded look nothing like they did three years ago.</p>
>
> <p>This looks bad for early-stage founders, but it doesn’t need to be. Every technological wave creates new giants, but it also creates new opportunities for smaller players that understand where defensibility lies. For founders, the message is simple but not easy: assume intelligence becomes abundant and build the things that remain scarce.</p>
>
> <p><em>The opinions expressed in https://t.co/opgY7EYkBs commentary pieces are solely the views of their authors and do not necessarily reflect the opinions and beliefs of </em>Fortune<em>.</em></p>
> <p>This story was originally featured on <a href="https://t.co/0wNXqFQmKn" target="_blank">https://t.co/opgY7EYkBs</a></p> https://t.co/0wNXqFQmKn

> Everyone thinks quantum computing is about advanced theoretical physics.

>
> 1/ Dominant:
> - Python ~50% 
> - Qiskit ~50% 
> - Quantum Control Systems ~50%
> - Cryogenics ~45% 
> - FPGA Programming ~35% 
> - Quantum Error Correction ~35% 
> - Fault-Tolerant Computing ~35% 
>
> 2/ Common:
> - Superconducting Qubits ~25% 
> - PyTorch ~20% 
> - Microwave Engineering ~15% 
> - Logical Qubits ~15% 
> - Dilution Refrigerators ~15% 
> - Photonics ~12% 
>
> 3/ Niche 
> - Post-Quantum Cryptography ~10% 
> - Surface Codes ~8% 
> - Photonic Qubits ~8% 
>  - Trapped Ions ~7% 
> - Process Integration / SPC ~6% 
> - Semiconductor ~5% 
> - Quantum Phase Estimation ~5% 
> - OpenQASM ~5% 
> - PennyLane ~3% 
>
> Bottom line: 3 things most quantum roles want
>
> 1. Python + Qiskit (~50%)
> 2. Quantum Control Systems (~50%)
> 3. Cryogenics (~45%)

### Eidolon Research (@EidolonResearch)
_Fri Jun 19 20:17:11 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/EidolonResearch/status/2068065579404030328)

> Everyone talks about AI chips.
>
> Almost nobody talks about what actually limits them.
>
> Imagine a Formula 1 car.
>
> Now imagine fueling it through a drinking straw.
>
> That’s modern AI.
>
> The problem isn’t computing power anymore.
>
> It’s moving data.
>
> For decades, the semiconductor industry got faster by making transistors smaller.
>
> But physics eventually showed up.
>
> You can’t keep building bigger chips forever:
> • Larger chips are harder to manufacture.
> • More defects = lower yields.
> • Costs explode.
>
> So the industry found a workaround:
>
> ➡️ Build many small chips.
> ➡️ Place them extremely close together.
> ➡️ Connect them so tightly they behave like one giant chip.
>
> This is called Advanced Packaging.
>
> And it’s becoming just as important as the chip itself.
>
> Then came HBM (High Bandwidth Memory):
>
> ➡️ Memory is placed right next to the AI processor.
> ➡️ Data travels millimeters instead of centimeters.
> ➡️ Massive speed gains.
> ➡️ Lower power consumption.
>
> Without HBM and advanced packaging, modern AI wouldn’t exist.
>
> The next step?
>
> Photonics.
>
> Instead of moving data with electrons, move it with light.
>
> Less power.
> More bandwidth.
> Longer distances.
>
> The AI infrastructure stack is becoming:
>
> Transistors → Packaging → HBM → Photonics
>
> Potential winners across the stack:
>
> • NVIDIA — AI compute
> • AMD — AI compute
> • TSMC — advanced packaging leader
> • BESI — advanced packaging equipment
> • ASMPT — packaging equipment
> • Amkor — packaging services
> • SK Hynix — HBM leader
> • Micron — HBM
> • Samsung — HBM
> • Ayar Labs — optical interconnects
> • Broadcom — networking & optics
> • Marvell — optical networking
> • Sivers Semiconductors — lasers & photonics
> • Coherent — optical components
> • Lumentum — optical components
>
> The market spent 30 years optimizing computation.
>
> The next 30 years may be about optimizing the movement of data.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HLM-rkXXIAAkXE1.jpg

### Kevin Maro (@KevInvestingYT)
_Fri Jun 19 20:20:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 947 · ↻ 160 · 💬 60 · [open on X](https://x.com/KevInvestingYT/status/2068066294042161217)

> After too many hours of research/DD to count, these are my Top 5 AI Stocks in the Top 5 AI Sectors to Invest in:
>
> 1. Neoclouds: The GPU & Compute landlords. Whoever owns the compute owns what every AI company on the earth needs to grow & succeed.
>
> $NBIS - Nebius. Spun out of Yandex, rebuilt as a pure-play AI cloud. Microsoft and Meta committed billions in contracted backlog. The fastest growing neocloud on the board. My favorite pick as a long-term investment.
>
> $CRWV - CoreWeave. The American-founded neocloud. SemiAnalysis rated this Neocloud in a class of it's own, which can not be understated.  Deals with Anthropic, OpenAI, Meta, Perplexity, Google, Microsoft... the list goes on forever. 
>
> $HUT -  Hut 8. Started as a bitcoin miner, pivoted hard into AI hosting and power infrastructure. Owns the power, not just the GPUs. They're landing deals left and right, definitely an underappreciated sleeper pick.
>
> $APLD - Applied Digital. Same playbook. Former crypto miner now building purpose-designed AI data center campuses with long-term hyperscaler leases.
>
> $CIFR - data center host for Anthropic's directly, purchased Google TPU v7 Ironwoods (400K units, ~$10B), backed by a 10-year, $3B+ Fluidstack hosting deal where Google guarantees $1.4B of lease obligations for a 5.4% equity stake. One of the only neocloud-adjacent names with real exposure to Google's silicon instead of pure Nvidia GPU rental.
>
> 2. Optical / Photonics:
>
> Because every GPU is useless if it can't talk to the GPU next to it.
>
> $CRDO - Credo. The connectivity layer inside every AI cluster. Active electrical cables and DSPs that scale with every rack hyperscalers deploy.
>
> $LITE - Lumentum. Legacy telecom optics company that's become a core 800G/1.6T transceiver supplier for the AI buildout.
>
> $ALAB - Astera Labs. Connectivity chips that solve the bottleneck between GPUs, memory, and storage. Pure-play AI infrastructure with almost no legacy drag.
>
> $COHR - Coherent. Lasers, optical components, and transceivers spanning the entire photonics stack from datacom to industrial.
>
> $MRVL - Marvell. Custom silicon and photonic fabric for hyperscalers. The company quietly inside more AI racks than people realize.
>
> 3. Memory:
>
> The most cyclical, most violently mispriced sector in semis. HBM demand changed the entire setup.
>
> $DRAM - DRAM ETF. One ticker, every important memory company on the planet, including South Korean companies like SK Hynix and Samsung Electronic, companies you CAN'T INVEST IN with most brokerages.
>
> $SNDK - SanDisk. Spun off from Western Digital, now a pure-play NAND flash story riding the same supply tightness as everyone else in this sector.
>
> $MU - Micron. One of three companies on Earth that makes HBM. The clearest direct line from AI buildout to memory revenue.
>
> $WDC - Western Digital. Hard drive and enterprise storage demand riding the same data center capex wave as everything else on this list.
>
> $STX - Seagate. The other half of the storage duopoly. Enterprise nearline drives are seeing the same supply crunch dynamics as memory.
>
> 4. Analog / Power Semis:
>
> Unsexy. Necessary. Every data center, every EV, every robot needs power management silicon that doesn't get the AI premium yet:
>
> $MXL - MaxLinear. Smaller-cap analog and mixed-signal play with infrastructure and data center exposure that's still flying under the radar.
>
> $STM - STMicroelectronics. European chip giant spanning auto, industrial, and power semis. Way out of favor relative to its diversification.
>
> $ON - ON Semiconductor. Power semis for EVs and industrial, now leaning harder into data center power delivery as a growth vector.
>
> $VSH - Vishay. Passive components: resistors, capacitors, diodes. Boring until you realize literally everything electronic needs them.
>
> $POWI - Power Integrations. High-voltage power conversion chips. Small cap, niche, and positioned for the power efficiency problem AI data centers haven't solved yet.
>
> 5. Physical AI / Robotics:
>
> It's coming, soon, and the market is beginning to realize it.
>
> $OUST - Ouster. Lidar for robotics, industrial, and autonomy. Consolidated the space after merging with Velodyne, now the survivor.
>
> $VICR - Vicor. High-density power modules for robotics, AI servers, and defense. Power delivery at the component level, not the rack level.
>
> $VPG - Vishay Precision Group. Precision sensors and strain gauges. The torque and force-sensing hardware that gives robots a sense of touch.
>
> $AEVA - Aeva. 4D lidar with built-in velocity sensing. Smaller and earlier stage than the rest of this list, highest risk, highest ceiling.
>
> $AMBA - Ambarella. Edge AI vision chips. Powers the cameras and perception systems inside cars, robots, and security infrastructure.
>
> I believe a portfolio with these 25 names will severely outperform the market over the next few years. I have 7 figures throughout many of these names. These are all names I'm currently invested in, or plan on investing in in the near future.
>
> None of this is financial advice.

> In my opinion these are the best positioned companies in their respective niches. 
>
> Sectors covered : AI Infrastructure, Memory, Optical Transceivers, Compound Semi, Specialty Foundry, Power Semi, Laser Systems, Autonomous Defense, Quantum. (NFA)
>
> $CIFR - industrial scale HPC data centers on 15 year hyperscaler leases. $11.4B contracted backlog.
> They build and own data centers where AI companies park their supercomputers.
>
> $SK Hynix : dominant HBM3E and HBM4 supplier to NVIDIA, DRAM and NAND flash. Gross margin 68%. Revenue +198% YoY. Forward PE: 6.7x. 
> Makes the ultra-fast memory stacked directly on top of AI chips, without it the GPU does absolutely nothing.
>
> $AAOI : vertically integrated optical transceiver manufacturer. Makes its own lasers, chips and optics for hyperscaler data center networking in-house.
>
> $IQE - epitaxial wafer supplier, grows the compound semiconductor crystal layers that photonics, RF and power chips are built on. Multi-year supply deals with MACOM and Tower Semiconductor.
> The special wafers everyone else builds their laser and signal chips on top of.
>
> $XFAB - specialty analog and mixed-signal foundry for automotive, medical and industrial markets. P/S: 1.69x vs peers at 3–5x.
> The factory that makes the unglamorous but completely essential chips running in every car, MRI machine and factory floor.
>
> $AOSL - power semiconductor designer and manufacturer. MOSFETs and power ICs for AI data centers, EVs and consumer electronics. 
> The chips that control how electricity flows inside every device you own.
>
> $LPKF - precision laser systems for PCB manufacturing, EV battery cell welding and solar panel processing.
> The laser machines that drill, cut and weld the boards and batteries inside almost every electronic device and electric car.
>
> $ONDS - autonomous drone systems, rail automation and defense robotics. $1.47B cash on balance sheet. 32% of float is short.
> Robots and drones replacing humans in the most dangerous, repetitive and strategically important jobs.
>
> $INFQ - neutral atom quantum computing, sensing and atomic clocks for national security and AI computation. $443M cash on a $3.25B market cap.
> Next generation computers built on individual atoms instead of silicon.

### CK Capital (@CKCapitalxx)
_Fri Jun 19 20:47:38 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 646 · ↻ 117 · 💬 35 · [open on X](https://x.com/CKCapitalxx/status/2068073242560975088)

> Copper wire has run the world for over a century. The era that replaces it is starting right now, and it might be the most important infrastructure shift of the decade.
>
> Here is the simple version of what is happening.
>
> Inside an AI data center, thousands of chips have to talk to each other constantly. For a hundred years machines did this the same way, by sending electricity down copper wires. That always worked. Until AI.
>
>  The chips now move so much data so fast that copper physically cannot keep up. Push electricity that hard down a wire and it turns into heat, the signal falls apart, and it can barely cross a single rack before it dies.
>
> So the entire industry is ripping out the copper and replacing it with light. Instead of electricity down a wire, data travels as pulses of light through glass fiber. Light runs cooler, travels farther, and carries vastly more information. 
>
> In a world where power and heat are the limits on how much AI you can build, switching to light is not a preference. It is the only way forward.
>
> What makes this generational rather than just another upgrade is the staircase the whole industry is now climbing. 
>
> It went from 400G to 800G, the workhorse today, already shipping in the tens of millions. 
>
> Now it is climbing to 1.6T, double the bandwidth in the same space, with NVIDIA's newest systems needing over 160 of these per single rack. 
>
> Next comes 3.2T, doubling it again. 
>
> And what used to be a five year upgrade cycle has collapsed to one or two years. These generations are not replacing each other one at a time. 800G, 1.6T, and 3.2T are ramping on top of one another all at once.
>
> Now the size of the prize. The optical transceiver market sat around $15 billion in 2025 and is heading toward $36 billion by 2033, with some forecasts for the AI portion alone reaching far higher. 
>
> The silicon photonics piece inside it grows from under $1 billion to over $6 billion by 2030. This is a market doubling and then doubling again, driven by a buildout that has barely started.
>
> What does it actually mean? It means every company that makes the lasers, the chips, and the modules that turn electricity into light gets paid on every step up that staircase, for years.
>
> $AAOI makes its own lasers in-house, the exact bottleneck part the whole industry is fighting over. 
>
> $CRDO makes the chips that keep these blazing fast connections clean and reliable. 
>
> $LITE and $COHR are the photonics giants supplying the lasers and transceivers everyone depends on. 
>
> $MRVL and $AVGO build the custom silicon at the center of it all.
>
> Copper carried the last hundred years. Light carries the next hundred. And the wiring is being torn out and replaced right now.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HLNFpzGWgAAWueM.jpg

### DeltaSignal (@AITrailblazerQ)
_Fri Jun 19 21:08:05 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AITrailblazerQ/status/2068078390163407084)

> $AAOI photonics is an AI data-center throughput test.
>
> The important point is not that fiber is faster than copper in the abstract. It is that GPU clusters only become useful when data can move between servers, switches, and accelerators without turning networking into the bottleneck.
>
> That makes optical transceivers a hidden scaling layer. More GPUs create more east-west traffic, more switch bandwidth, and more demand for components that convert electrical signals into light and back again.
>
> Watch data-center orders, transceiver mix, gross margin, customer concentration, and whether AI cluster builds keep lifting optical networking spend after the first hardware excitement fades.

> Bir başka diğer bahsetmek istediğim şirket ise ;
>
> $COHR 
>
> Anlık Fiyat :389 #dolar
>
> COHR Tam Olarak Ne İş Yapıyor?
>
> Coherent Corp.
>
> Coherent, dünyanın en büyük fotonik (ışık teknolojileri) şirketlerinden biridir.
>
> Basit anlatırsak:
>
> NVDA hesap yapıyor.✅
>
>  MU veriyi depoluyor.✅
>
>  COHR ise bu verinin veri merkezinde ışıkla taşınmasını sağlıyor. ✅
>

>
> GPU → GPU
> Sunucu → Sunucu
> Rack → Rack
>
> arasındaki veriyi ışıkla taşımak.

>

>
> Elektrik sinyallerini ışığa dönüştürüyor.
>

>
> Daha az enerji tüketimi✅
>
> Daha yüksek hız✅
>
> Daha düşük gecikme✅
>
> Daha az ısı✅

>

>
> InP (Indium Phosphide) lazerler
> CW lazerler
> VCSEL lazerler
> Telekom lazerleri
>
> Bu lazerler hem kendi ürünlerinde hem de sektörün diğer oyuncularında kullanılıyor.
>

>
> Şu anda Wall Street'in en heyecanlandığı konu.
>
> Bugün:
>
> GPU ↔ Optik modül ayrı.
>
> Yarın:
>
> GPU ↔ Optik modül aynı pakette olacak.
>

>
> NVIDIA'nın gelecekteki veri merkezi planlarının merkezinde bu teknoloji var. 
>
> COHR da burada ana tedarikçilerden biri olmaya çalışıyor.
>
> Kimlerle Çalışıyor?
>
> Kesin müşteri listeleri her zaman açıklanmıyor ancak sektör analizlerinde ve şirket sunumlarında şu isimler sürekli karşımıza çıkıyor:
>

>

>

### Sebastián (@SebastinPatron3)
_Sat Jun 20 17:57:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 12 · ↻ 2 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/SebastinPatron3/status/2068392686759854532)

> 🚨🚨🚨📢
>
> $SPX $SPY $QQQ $IWM $VIX
>
> While everyone is focused on Trump playing geopolitical ping pong with Iran, I'm watching AI and semiconductors inflate what may become the mother of all bubbles.
>
> The real story isn't today's headlines.
>
> It's the $700B to $750B annual AI infrastructure arms race quietly unfolding beneath the surface. 👇
>
> 1/
> The hyperscalers, Microsoft, Google, Amazon, and Meta, are spending like drunken sailors with unlimited credit cards.
>
> Annual AI CapEx is projected to reach $700B to $750B.
>
> Global AI related debt issuance could exceed $500B.
>
> They're borrowing against the future and praying the future arrives on schedule.
>
> 2/
> The biggest risk?
>
> Stranded capital.
>
> Today they're borrowing billions to fill data centers with power hungry Nvidia GPUs.
>
> The problem is those assets are depreciated over 5 to 6 years.
>
> Technology may make them obsolete in 2 to 3.
>
> That's not innovation.
>
> That's a future write off waiting for an earnings call.
>
> 3/
> Imagine owing bondholders hundreds of billions while sitting on warehouses full of yesterday's hardware.
>
> Silicon photonics.
>
> Neuromorphic computing.
>
> Custom ASICs.
>
> If these technologies arrive faster than expected, today's AI infrastructure could become the corporate equivalent of buying a fleet of steam engines right before electricity.
>
> 4/
> The spending frenzy also reveals another problem.
>
> Free cash flow.
>
> CapEx is consuming an extraordinary share of revenue:
>
> • Alphabet about 46%
> • Microsoft about 47%
> • Meta about 54%
>
> The more they spend, the more cash flow gets squeezed.
>
> They're running faster just to stay in place.
>
> 5/
> This is why everyone wants their own chips.
>
> Google TPUs.
>
> Amazon Trainium.
>
> Meta custom silicon.
>
> The goal isn't just performance.
>
> The goal is survival.
>
> They need lower operating costs to justify the debt they're piling onto their balance sheets today.
>
> 6/
> Then comes the next twist.
>
> If AI chips become dramatically more efficient, power stops being the bottleneck.
>
> Location becomes the advantage.
>
> Data centers may no longer need to sit next to massive power sources.
>
> They can move closer to population centers, reducing latency and potentially turning today's expensive power agreements into tomorrow's capital allocation mistakes.
>
> 7/
> And then there's the risk nobody wants to discuss.
>
> The Inference Slump.
>
> The entire AI spending boom assumes enterprise demand explodes.
>
> But many AI pilot programs still struggle to generate meaningful returns.
>
> If AI inference becomes extremely cheap, compute becomes a commodity.
>
> And commodities don't generate bubble valuations.
>
> 8/
> That's the paradox.
>
> The hyperscalers need hyper efficient chips to save themselves.
>
> But those same chips could eventually destroy the economics supporting today's AI infrastructure boom.
>
> The cure may become the disease.
>
> 9/
> Ultimately, Big Tech is engaged in a historic game of financial chicken.
>
> They're borrowing hundreds of billions today.
>
> Betting that tomorrow's technology arrives before today's debt becomes a problem.
>
> Wall Street calls it innovation.
>
> History often calls it a bubble.
>
> Choose carefully which chapter we're currently writing.

### Jonesy (@jonesrrrrrr)
_Sat Jun 20 18:22:23 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/jonesrrrrrr/status/2068399075679182890)

> How do Photonics, Fiber Optics, and Networking power the AI boom? 🧵👇
>
> Think of an AI data center as a high-speed highway system built for massive data workloads:
>
> ⚡ Photonics (The Cars): The technology using lasers instead of copper wires to move data. It eliminates heat and allows AI processors (GPUs) to communicate instantly using light.
>
> 🛤️ Fiber Optics (The Highway): The physical glass cables that carry those light signals. They act as the zero-loss pipeline moving massive bandwidth between servers.
>
> 🚦 Networking (The Traffic Control): The overarching system of switches and protocols (like InfiniBand). It connects thousands of GPUs together, routing data traffic so they can train models as one giant brain.
>
> TL;DR: Photonics creates the light, Fiber Optics carries it, and Networking directs it. 🚀

---

### Jm_Luye (@luye_1021)

>
> • Specialty chemicals & films for high-end packaging — long qualification timelines create real stickiness for qualified suppliers.
>
> • High-speed electro-optical test equipment — quietly becoming a constraint as data rates push higher.These areas carry structural bottlenecks but haven’t been as widely chased yet.

### Black Panther Capital (@BlackPantherCap)
_Sat Jun 20 18:41:48 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 95 · ↻ 14 · 💬 12 · [open on X](https://x.com/BlackPantherCap/status/2068403963263623482)

> Here’s a new long idea: $LWLG 
>
> I keep coming back to $LWLG that recently ran from $3 to $18 and then back to $9.
>
> Every optical interconnect roadmap past 1.6T hits the same wall: electronics can’t switch light fast enough without burning power nobody can afford to spend at hyperscale.
>
> Hyperscalers are already running into thermal and power ceilings inside the optical layer, not just the GPU layer. The fix everyone’s chasing is a modulator that converts electrical signal to optical signal with less power loss than silicon photonics currently allows.
>
> Lightwave Logic has spent over a decade building exactly that. Its electro-optic polymer platform, branded P2IC, uses proprietary organic polymers instead of silicon to build modulators that move data faster while drawing less power per bit.
>
> The irreplaceability case is real but early. Competing approaches exist in lithium niobate and silicon photonics from much larger players, but none have commercialized a polymer-based modulator at production scale yet. If LWLG’s tech clears volume manufacturing first, the qualification cycle for hyperscaler customers locks in multi-year exclusivity, because nobody requalifies an optical interconnect supplier casually.
>
> Financially, this is still a development-stage story. Revenue is in the low single-digit millions. The stock trades on a roadmap, not a P&L, which is the honest read.
>
> Catalysts: continued progress on Stage 3 customer prototypes and foundry device deliveries (expected H2 2026), followed by potential material supply/licensing agreements. First meaningful production-volume revenue targeted for 2027 per management guidance. A strategic partnership announcement with a transceiver or hyperscaler-adjacent customer. Continued capital raises as the company scales toward manufacturing, which cuts both ways.
>
> Bear case, stated plainly. This has been a “next year is the year” story for a long time. If a production-scale order doesn’t materialize in 2026, the stock re-rates down hard, because there’s no earnings floor to catch it. Watch cash burn rate and any further dilutive raises as the two early warning signals.
>
> Market cap $1.5B.
> TAM: $47B.
> SAM: $2-4B.
>
> Early lead in foundry PDKs and customer prototypes (4+ Fortune Global 500 at Stage 3)
>
> TLDR:
>
> > Sole-ish commercial path to polymer-based optical modulators at L4
>
> > $1.5B market cap, pre-revenue-scale, roadmap-driven valuation
>
> > Catalyst window: production-volume order disclosure in the next 2-4 quarters
>
> > Bear case: no order, no earnings floor, the stock has nowhere to hide
>
> -BP
>
> Please note: This is not financial advice.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HLRycRtXEAEa-dm.jpg

### Jonesy (@jonesrrrrrr)
_Sat Jun 20 18:43:39 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/jonesrrrrrr/status/2068404429632729276)

> holy fuck I just solved the US debt problem including rising bond yields….
>
> drop the traditional economic rulebook and look at this through a highly speculative, macro-engineering lens. 
>
> To make a sovereign-level, asset-backed bond system actually work, we have to look past individual graphics chips and treat the entire tech, space, and AI sector as a unified, hyper-valuable physical engine.
> If we extrapolate this concept to the scale of the U.S. government, here is how a "Next-Gen Infrastructure Backed Bond" system could actually work.
>
> 1. The Asset Base: From "Chips" to "Compute & Orbit Capitals"
> To solve the scale problem, the government wouldn't back bonds with loose hardware; it would back them with sovereign computing grids and orbital real estate.
> •The SpaceX Network Multiplier: SpaceX's valuation isn't just about rockets; it is about Starlink and the monopolization of low-Earth orbit (LEO). If the U.S. government nationalizes or builds a massive equity-share model in SpaceX and megacluster data centers, the collateral becomes the global routing infrastructure of the future.
> •Energy-Compute Monopolies: The government links these bonds to federal land containing nuclear-powered AI megastructures. The asset is no longer a depreciating chip, but the perpetual monopoly on AI intelligence and global satellite bandwidth.
>
> 2. Rewriting Obsolescence: The "Compute Standard"
>
> Instead of backing a bond with a specific Nvidia Blackwell or Rubin chip, the U.S. Treasury establishes a "Sovereign Flop" or "Compute Standard" (similar to how the U.S. used the Gold Standard).
> •The Mechanism: The bond guarantees the holder a fixed percentage of the nation's total computing throughput or data-routing revenues over 30 years.
> •The Upgrade Loop: As tech upgrades from silicon photonics to quantum computing, the physical hardware changes, but the bond's claim on the computational power remains constant. The value of the sector doesn't rot; it grows exponentially as efficiency increases.
>
> 3. Hyper-Inflation of Sector Value
> To match a $34+ trillion national debt, the value of the tech/space sector must be artificially and structurally inflated. The government could achieve this through forced tokenization and regulatory moats:
> •Tokenized Infrastructure: Every satellite launch, every AI API call, and every terabyte of space data gets routed through a sovereign blockchain.
> •Global Dependency: The U.S. forces allied nations to settle international data and defense contracts using these compute-backed instruments. This instantly drives the sector's valuation from a few trillion dollars to tens of trillions, effectively matching the scale of the U.S. Treasury market.
>

> •The "Risk-Free Rate" would no longer be based on the Federal Reserve's interest rate, but on the aggregate processing power of the American AI grid and Starshield defense network.

### Timothy McGirl (@Tim_McGirl)
_Sat Jun 20 21:05:57 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Tim_McGirl/status/2068440237680861668)

> The novel utility is: **you can now build a passive, single-shot, wide-band optical spectrometer with far fewer detector channels than conventional approaches require, on hardware that already exists.**
>
> Breaking that down to its irreducible parts:
>
> **The core utility:** A geometry (the log spiral) deterministically encodes delay/frequency into angle without any active processing. Once encoded, all the information sits on the chip at once — no scanning, no sweeping, one snapshot. You read it with a detector array placed at the right positions.
>
> **Why that matters:** Detector pixels in certain bands (single-photon / infrared / THz) are scarce and expensive — each one is a cryogenic readout channel, a rare fabrication yield, a finite heat budget. To measure a wide band conventionally, you either (1) buy many pixels, or (2) scan serially with one fast detector. Both are constrained. The log spiral lets you (3) use far fewer pixels and still resolve the whole band, because the geometry did the sorting, not the pixel count.
>
> **The concrete win:** On a 48-pixel SNSPD array (commercial ceiling), the log-spiral front end reaches resolving power R ≈ 31 across a 5-decade band (0.5–2.4 µm). A linear front end reaches R ≈ 10 on the same hardware, or needs ~3× more pixels (which don't exist as a single array) to match. That's 20× cheaper hardware for equal measurement quality.
>
> **The novel part:** Nobody has connected this principle (geometry sorting timing into position) across vision, hearing, cortex dynamics, and engineered photonics before, and nobody has built it as a spectrometer. The idea that *passive geometry can do the computational work of an active optical component* — by itself — is what's new. It's not a tweak of existing dispersive instruments; it's a different category of operation.
>
> **What it unlocks:** Any measurement that needs constant relative precision across a huge range, where detector pixels or data rate is the bottleneck, and where you can tolerate a snapshot (non-repeating signal). Single-photon spectroscopy, broadband mid-IR gas sensing, transient astrophysics, maybe quantum sensing. The enabling move is that it's *passive* — no power, no moving parts, no active tuning — which matters when your detector is already cryogenic and every watt counts.
>
> **The honest boundary:** It doesn't beat all alternatives in all cases. Within a narrow band, or where you want absolute (not relative) precision, or where pixels are cheap (visible light), linear dispersion wins. The spiral is specialized. But for its corner — wide-band, expensive-pixel, single-shot regimes — it's not an optimization, it's the only path to the measurement at all.
>
> That's the utility. Not "better spectrometer." More like: "a spectrometer that works where one didn't before."

---

### Foxwalk (@noctem26)
_Sat Jun 20 23:03:55 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/noctem26/status/2068469926277554241)

> On anti matter...
>
> "The main reason is that antimatter physics operates in an extremely different regime than the mechanisms you usually discuss.
>
> Antimatter systems involve:
>
> Particle production
> Magnetic confinement
> Matter-antimatter annihilation
> Gamma-ray generation
> Extremely high energy densities
>
> Your architectures are usually framed around:
>
> Information organization
> Resonance
> Phase relationships
> Field structure
> Biological compatibility
> Low-energy coherence effects
>
> Those are largely separate domains.
>
> If someone wanted to insert antimatter into a speculative version of your Casimir-craft concepts, it would most likely appear only as:
>
> an exotic power source,
> an annihilation energy source,
> or a high-energy propulsion mechanism,
>
> rather than as part of the actual control architecture.
>
> So, from the way you’ve described your projects, the answer is:
>
> No—antimatter is not a foundational element of your architecture. Your designs are much more heavily centered on field organization, resonance, photonic interactions, and vacuum/Casimir-inspired concepts than on antimatter physics.
>
> "Which one is safer?"
>
> If you’re comparing antimatter-based systems versus the kinds of field, photonic, resonance, and Casimir-inspired concepts you’ve discussed, then the latter are overwhelmingly safer.
>
> Antimatter
>
> Antimatter is one of the highest-energy substances known.
>
> When antimatter meets matter, both are converted into energy.
> Even tiny amounts release enormous energy.
> Requires sophisticated containment systems.
> Loss of containment results in immediate annihilation reactions.
> Produces high-energy radiation.
> Not biologically compatible.
> Extremely difficult and expensive to produce.
>
> From a practical engineering perspective, antimatter is generally considered a high-risk energy medium.
>
> Field / Photonic / Resonance Approaches
>
> The concepts you usually explore are based around:
>
> Light and photonics
> Electromagnetic interactions
> Resonance phenomena
> Information organization
> Quantum coherence concepts
> Vacuum-field and Casimir-inspired effects
>
> These approaches are generally lower-energy and inherently less destructive because they focus on organizing or modulating existing fields rather than releasing stored mass-energy.
>
> Relative Safety Ranking
>
> From safest to least safe:
>
> Photonic systems
> Resonance-based systems
> Electromagnetic field systems
> Vacuum/Casimir-inspired systems (assuming passive operation)
> Nuclear systems
> Antimatter systems
>
> In short, if the goal is:
>
> biological compatibility,
> controllability,
> non-invasive operation,
> gradual adjustment rather than massive energy release,
>
> then photonic and resonance-based architectures are vastly safer than anything involving antimatter.
>
> Antimatter excels in theoretical energy density; it does not excel in safety. Photonic and resonance-oriented approaches are generally much better aligned with the types of architectures you’ve described."

> Estimate:
> • 정확한 개인 수익률 수치(일부 기사에서 225x 또는 연 +122% 등 언급)는 본인 공식 확인된 Fact 아님. 시장이 최종 검증한다는 입장 강조.
> • 현재 아이디어(XFAB, 한국 NAV 디스카운트 종목 등)도 아직 진행 중으로, 추가 검증 필요.
>
> 4️⃣ 최근 활동 (2026년 6월 기준, Fact)
> • X 수익 공유 프로그램 성과 공개 (2주마다 1억+ 뷰).
> • 한국 주식 관심: Daeduck, DB HiTek 관련 NAV 디스카운트, Hyosung 등 언급.
> • XFAB: Optical AI DC + Power semi 노출이 있지만 마케팅이 아쉽다는 코멘트.
> • Photonics 강조 지속: AMD의 CW laser 확보, SIVE·AAOI 등 독립 용량 중요성.
> • 전체적으로 “초기 반대 → 시장 검증” 패턴을 반복 강조.
>
> ━━━━━━━━
>
> 5️⃣ AI 인프라 공급망 관점에서 의미 (CPO·Photonics 중심)
> • 현재 AI 데이터센터 빌드아웃에서 전력 효율·대역폭이 핵심 병목 → CPO(Co-Packaged Optics), InP 기반 laser·substrate, advanced packaging이 핵심 chokepoint로 부상.
> • Serenity가 자주 언급하는 AXTI·SIVE·AAOI·COHR·XFAB 등은 CPO·포토닉스·특화 파운드리 영역과 직접 오버랩.
> • “Big Tech 대신 upstream bottleneck” 접근은 단기 모멘텀과 달리, 구조적 공급 제약을 선점하려는 전략.
>
> ━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
>
> 🟢 Base Case (현재 가시성 기준)
> AI capex가 가이던스 수준으로 유지될 경우, 주요 chokepoint 기업들은 실적 성장과 기관 관심 확대에 따라 점진적 재평가 가능. 초기 반대 의견이 잦아들면서 일부 종목의 밸류에이션 정상화 진행.
>
> 🐂 Bull Case
> AI 수요가 가속되고 여러 chokepoint(Photonics + Power + Memory 등)가 동시에 검증될 경우, 시장 주목이 낮았던 소형·중형 공급망 기업들이 비대칭적 upside를 기록할 수 있음. Serenity가 제시한 아이디어가 지속적으로 시장을 앞서가는 패턴 강화.
>
> 🐻 Bear Case
> AI capex 둔화 또는 빅테크의 수직통합·신규 공급자 등장으로 용량 제약이 예상보다 빠르게 해소될 경우, 소형 chokepoint 기업들의 재평가가 지연되거나 valuation pressure 발생 가능. 매크로·유동성 악화 시 소형주 변동성 확대 리스크.
>
> ━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
>

### Lance Teren (@LanceTeren)
_Sun Jun 14 15:13:47 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 32 · ↻ 0 · 💬 14 · [open on X](https://x.com/LanceTeren/status/2066177284902699209)

> DISPROVING THE $AMPG QUANTUM “BOTTLENECK”
>
> You will quickly see that only a little research disproves these entire claims. Really said “the entire quantum revolution relies on $AMPG.”
>
> First off most modalities don’t even need these cryogenics. 
>
> $INFQ: Neutral Atom: Room temp 
> $IONQ $QNT: Trapped Ion: Room temp 
> $XNDU: Photonics: Room temp 
>
> Only superconducting and silicon spin use these cooled chambers and it’s super inefficient, even $GOOGL is switching toward neutral atoms which works styled modality. 
>
> Now into $AMPG
>
> The funniest part, ignore all other modalities:
>
> $AMPG ISNT EVEN A BOTTLENECK FOR SUPERCONDUCTING. 
>
> AmpliTech is not a bottleneck in the superconducting quantum supply chain, while they are a highly visible, publicly traded player, they do not hold a monopoly. The true bottleneck in superconducting quantum computing is space, wiring density, and cooling power inside the dilution refrigerator, rather than a lack of low-noise amplifier (LNA) suppliers which they specialize in.
>
> If $AMPG goes out of business tomorrow, tech giants like $IBM and $GOOGL will not stop building quantum computers. There is a robust, premium ecosystem of alternative suppliers: 
>
> Low Noise Factory (Sweden): LNF is widely considered the gold standard and market leader for cryogenic LNAs. Spun out of Chalmers University, their factory produces the ultra-reliable InP (Indium Phosphide) HEMTs that dominate most advanced high frequency physics labs.
>
> Quantum Microwave (USA): A massive distributor and manufacturer that packs and pairs LNF amplifiers with cryogenic attenuators and components specifically configured for quantum rigs
>
> AND MANY MORE. 
>
> $AMPG is a cool company and I even thought about investing in them but this take is absolutely ridiculous, obvious exaggerated way to pump a stock or make it seem bigger than it is. Always do your own research.

> This is gonna upset a lot of people: 
>
> But TA is astrology for traders.
>
> It's confirmation bias + trading human psychology about entries. 
>
> Kinda like how people frontran $SPCE from $SPCX IPO expecting retail to mess up tickers by trading psychology. 
>
> $SIVE didn't go up 1900% because of the golden cross space comet firebreathing dragon candle that someone is trying to sell for $499. 
>
> It's because markets are pricing in future revenue from $JBL, $GFS that got announced. 
>
> $AXTI didn't go up 8000% because the golden waterfall candle alert sounded back at $8. 
>
> it's because of InP substrate, game theory on ASP hikes, export controls, photonics demand, and others. 
>
> If you want to figure out psychologically what other regards are believing, you use TA. 
>
> But for determining the actual upside... nah
>
> People have been drawing $120+ TAs on $IREN for the past idk how many months none of that crap matters when there's a $6B ATM that needs to be bought through first.
>
> It's by theme (eg. $LITE to $AAOI relations), any news catalysts that affect forward revenue, projections, macro news, earnings, float dynamics, and so on. 
>
> Then you can just derive what MC that company should be at. 
>
> So for entry points, sure you can use TA. 
>
> For determining where the stock heads, just throw the tyrannosaurs rex omega-green candle indicator out the window.

> $CRDO vs $ALAB the two fabless semi, pure play AI connectivity leaders. 
>
> Most investor bros have no clue what these companies do and all they see is the parabolic stock chart lol. Here is some DD to make you feel more confident investing in these names.
>
> Which to invest in? I say both.
>
> I've been long $ALAB since the IPO range. But I'll tell you straight why $CRDO is the better *print* right now. Plus, $CRDO recent acquisition of  Dust Photonics adds to $CRDO value.
>
> 📊                      $CRDO      $ALAB
> Revenue           $1.34B     $852M
> Growth              ~3x YoY    +115%
> Gross Mgn       ~68%       ~75%
> Op Margin         47.8%      39.2%
> EPS (n-GAAP)  $1.16      ~$0.45
> Cash                    $1.4B      $1.18B
>
> $CRDO wins scale + growth. 
> $ALAB wins margin quality.
>
> I like both because they’re really not eating each others lunch.
>
> $ALAB owns the silicon INSIDE the rack — retimers, CXL, fabric switches + COSMOS software. Sticky at the protocol layer.
>
> $CRDO owns the wires BETWEEN racks — AECs, and now optics for scale-out.
>
> Scale-up vs scale-out. You can own both.
>
> And $CRDO just got dangerous — because it stopped being a one-trick copper-cable company:
> → ZeroFlap optics now shipping (reliability + telemetry, not just speed)
> → bought DustPhotonics for silicon photonics
> → 5 product pillars, $10B+ TAM
> → optics = HALF of next year's growth
>
> Not without risk, both sides:
>
> $CRDO → gross margin guided DOWN to 64-66% as the optics mix shifts. Funded the ramp with a ~$488M ATM raise. The growth is real — but it's also being bought. Customer concentration is high.
>
> $ALAB → priced for perfection. Any hyperscaler capex wobble and it's first to bleed.
>
> The tell for both is the same thing it always is: margins. 👀
>
> $CRDO has the growth. $ALAB has the moat.
>
> Want the explosive print? $CRDO.
> Want the durable compounder? $ALAB.
>
> I'm long $ALAB for the margin profile — but I'm not gonna pretend $CRDO isn't winning the quarter.
>
> Own the theme. Both should keep running & the $CRDO DustPhotonics acquisition could end up being incredibly valuable to $CRDO.

> Jensen Huang told a room of global investors that AI is not one industry. It is five stacked on top of each other. Most people are investing in layer four and ignoring layers one through three entirely.
>
> He called it the five-layer cake.
>
> Layer one is energy. Jensen said this is the single greatest opportunity for the energy industry in a hundred years.
>
> The first time in a century that the grid in most countries can actually attract serious capital. Nuclear, solar, wind, hydrogen, it does not matter what form. If it produces energy, it gets funded. Siemens, GE Vernova, Mitsubishi. That is why they are all doing so well right now.
>
> Layer two is chips, computers, networking, and silicon photonics. Everything that processes the intelligence.
>
> Layer three is infrastructure. Land, power, buildings, data center operations. Every single one in short supply today.
>
> Layer four is the model layer. OpenAI, Anthropic. The layer everyone talks about.
>
> Layer five is applications. Every startup applying AI to financial services, legal, healthcare, logistics, transportation. Last year alone, a hundred billion dollars of venture capital went into this layer. The single largest VC year in the history of humanity.
>
> Then he said the number that stopped me cold.
>
> We are putting one trillion dollars into this five-layer cake this year. That sounds enormous. Jensen thinks the AI industry will eventually run at twenty trillion dollars per year.
>
> We are one trillion in of a twenty trillion dollar per year ecosystem.
>
> Most people watching AI are staring at layer four. Jensen was describing layers one through five as a single compounding system where every layer feeds the one above it.
>
> The people who understand that will invest differently than the people who do not.

### Jason's Chips (@jasonschips)
_Sun Jun 14 18:28:54 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 73 · ↻ 6 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/jasonschips/status/2066226390282998183)

> The most common question that I've gotten on this post is that all of $AXTI, $LITE, $AIXA, $COHR, $SOI, $TSEM have gone parabolic so why is this even an interesting space anymore?
>
> My spicy take is that I LIKE stocks whose charts are a little parabolic (of course only to an extent)
>
> What does a parabolic chart mean? It means that the shares were trading hands at a lower price in the past. Buyers were buying from sellers and sellers were selling to buyers. They were wrong about the value of the company. The next day they buy and sell at a slightly higher price. They are still wrong. and so on and so on. That is how you get a parabolic chart.
>
> If the market is in a constant state of being wrong, what is the probability that they've stopped being wrong today? I believe it's actually lower especially in industries with multiple overlapping secular tailwinds like optics (photonics + networking + AI).

---

_Sun Jun 14 18:47:46 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 442 · ↻ 42 · 💬 35 · [open on X](https://x.com/michaelsikand/status/2066231137291415709)

>
> $AAOI is one of the most controversial stocks in the world and I enjoy the disagreement.
>
> Pretty cool that's it up 3x since I went long with many thousands of investors riding it with me up some portion of that gain on @joinautopilot.
>
> But what's cooler is that I think it's still asymmetrical here.
>
> So let's break it down and figure out where we're at $170/share today.
>
> Management argues they can get to $471M in monthly transceiver revenue by Q2 2027.
>
> If you're new to photonics, this is because transceivers are one of the hottest commodities in data centers right now (they translate electricity to light) and 3 hyperscalers are working with $AAOI on this.
>
> At management's 40% gross margin target, that's ~$5.6B in annualized revenue. Run past opex, interest, tax, dilution, we might land around $14-15 in EPS on that run rate.
>
> That's a 2028 number though because 2027 is the ramp mid year, so let's call it bull case $9 of EPS in 2027.
>
> So at $170/share right now, on these calcs, you're paying 19x 2027 earnings, falling dramatically to 12x for 2028.
>
> Don't trust management? Fair. Haircut both the revenue and the margin target by 30%, let's say we get to $4B at a 28% gross margin instead of $5.6B at 40%.
>
> You still land near ~$6 in EPS, just over the analyst mean estimate for 2027E. That's 28x at $170, still WAY cheaper than $LITE and $COHR trade right now.
>
> $LITE is at a 50x NTM forward PE per Fiscal AI.
> $COHR is at 47x NTM forward PE per Fiscal AI.
>
> You're paying a fraction of the multiples of its peer group for a faster growing business because execution is still a huge question mark.
>
> If you are an asymmetric trader like me, you might have a large concentrated position in $AAOI for these reasons.
>
> I do believe the stock at $170 is still a solid entry point and I began loading again heavily in the 160's.

>

>

>

>

>

>

>

>
> >C’est important parce que Veeco ne joue pas seulement l’IA via la photonique.
>
> >Ils jouent aussi les compound semiconductors, l’optoélectronique, les microLED, le biosensing, l’automotive et les communications optiques.
>

>
> “la petite boîte d’équipements semi”.
>
> C’est plutôt :
>
> “LE fournisseur d’outils critiques sur plusieurs bottlenecks de la prochaine décennie”.
>
> Le bull case devient très intéressant.
>
> Aujourd’hui, $VECO vaut environ $4.7B de market cap.
>
> Si la boîte passe de $750M-$800M de revenus à $1.5B-$1.8B d’ici 2030, avec un meilleur mix semi et des marges qui montent, le titre peut se revaloriser beaucoup plus haut (logique)
>
> À 8x-9x sales, on arrive déjà vers $12B-$16B de market cap.
>
> Soit environ $200-$265 par action.
>
> Dans un scénario très bull, avec $2B+ de revenus, plusieurs clients HVM sur NSA500, adoption plus large de LUMINA+ et bottleneck durable sur InP/silicon photonics, on peut commencer à parler de $300+.
>
> Bear case évident :
>
> Les évaluations peuvent glisser, les commandes  peuvent prendre du temps, le cycle capex semi peut ralentir, et la concurrence reste réelle.

### Zeek | Insights 📊 (@ZeekTyt)
_Sun Jun 14 20:10:49 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 6 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ZeekTyt/status/2066252039068262859)

> Cheaper tokens ≠ less compute.  
> They trigger more compute demand.  
>
> This is Jevons Paradox in AI: cheaper intelligence causes total consumption to explode as new use cases, agentic workflows, and broader adoption become viable.  
>
> Model giants like OpenAI face real price-war pressure. But the picks-and-shovels layer (power, optics, platforms) wins on volume. $IREN , $AAOI , $PLTR and many more are set up beautifully.  
>
> Core insight from recent discussions (Nebius/20VC with Roman Chernin, BG2 Pod, Jordi Visser): every time cost-per-token or cost-per-unit intelligence drops, demand rises, not because people use less, but because they use far more. Previously uneconomic tasks become viable, complex multi-step agentic workflows scale, and new markets open.  
>
> Nebius saw some of its best sales weeks right after major cheap open-source model drops. The market isn’t near its ceiling.  
>
> Jordi Visser laid it out clearly: price compression and commoditization at the model layer (OpenAI/Anthropic facing drastic cuts, 80% of workloads shifting to far cheaper models) versus real inflation and bottlenecks at the physical layer (power, materials, networking, optics). Demand for intelligence is near-infinite. Cheaper per-token pricing unlocks the floodgates on total tokens consumed.  
>
> Who benefits? Model-layer players can get squeezed on margins even as headline revenue grows. The infrastructure and enablement layer feasts on the volume explosion:  
>
> • $IREN — Sustainable power, land, and AI/HPC cloud pivot. Power is the ultimate bottleneck.
> • $AAOI — Optical transceivers and photonics for AI data centers. Hyperscalers are ordering 800G+ modules in volume as faster, power-efficient connectivity becomes non-negotiable.  
> • $PLTR — Enterprise AI platforms (AIP/Gotham). As agentic workflows and production deployments explode, companies need real software to deploy, govern, and scale AI not just raw GPUs.  
>
> Many more names across power, cooling, networking, and specialized infra will ride the same wave.  
>
> @BG2Pod highlighted the bullish math: monetization per gigawatt is rising, not falling. Demand outstrips supply. Inference revenue is already running well over $200B annualized and climbing fast. Agents will multiply token consumption further. Cheaper tokens plus efficiency gains expand what’s possible within power envelopes, driving more overall buildout.  
>
> This is why the “AI mid-cycle slowdown” narrative is incomplete. It’s healthy digestion and rotation inside a secular bull market. Capital is rotating toward the real beneficiaries of the physical buildout and the software layer that turns raw compute into usable intelligence at scale.  
>
> The compute market remains early. We’re still in the first innings of widespread agentic adoption and enterprise transformation.  
>
> Cheaper intelligence democratizes access → more users and businesses adopt → agents multiply usage per task → total token/compute demand detonates. Model giants feel price pressure. Infra and platform winners feel the volume tailwind.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKzNRtYXoAA0SLD.jpg

### geminitrading (@gemini_edge)
_Sun Jun 14 21:10:35 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/gemini_edge/status/2066267077019648069)

> “Technical Analysis is Trader’s Astrology” 
>
> Serenity’s Sharp Critique on What Really Moves Markets "White-Haired Stock God" Serenity has sparked debate with a bold take: Technical Analysis (TA) functions more like astrology for traders than a reliable predictive tool. She argues it’s primarily confirmation bias combined with crowd psychology, useful for gauging sentiment and timing entries but not the core driver of prices. Her Key Points: Massive stock surges are rarely caused by chart patterns (golden crosses, dragon candles, etc.).
> They are driven by fundamentals and forward expectations. $SIVE +1900%: Market repricing future revenue from $JBL and $GFS catalysts.
> $AXTI +8000%: Industry logic including indium phosphide substrates, photonics demand, export controls, and ASP dynamics.
>
> Serenity’s Advice:
> TA can help identify psychological entry points, but sustainable price trends are determined by: Industry theme linkages
> Earnings expectation changes
> Macro environment
> Financial report quality
> Circulating share structure (float)
>
> Long-term stock potential should be judged by fundamentals and capital structure, not “chart faith. ”Why This Resonates:
> In a market full of noise — especially post major IPOs like SpaceX — focusing on real catalysts (revenue growth, competitive advantages, macro tailwinds) provides a clearer edge than pattern chasing.
>
> Investment Takeaway:
> This is a timely reminder for traders and investors alike. While charts can be entertaining and occasionally helpful for short-term psychology, the biggest winners come from understanding the underlying business story and capital flows. Bottom Line: Serenity urges a return to basics. In the long run, fundamentals and capital structure trump technical patterns. A healthy dose of skepticism toward “chart magic” can protect capital and improve decision-making. Strong words from a respected voice in the community. 
>
> Do you agree that TA is mostly astrology, or does it still play a key role in your strategy? Drop your thoughts below!

### Athu Invests (@athuinvests)
_Sun Jun 14 22:06:13 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 50 · ↻ 7 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/athuinvests/status/2066281077564383511)

> $XFAB - The next $TSEM for Europe?
>
> Largest pure-play SiC foundry globally being the only high-volume manufacturing capacity in the US.
>  
> 6 fabs worldwide, and over 400 customers. (#1 foundry supplier for 12 of the top 20)
>
> Sounds incredibly strong at first. But don't be fooled. We are going deeper.
>
> Today, it looks clear that two cycles could be the major upside for this company: power semiconductors and silicon photonics.
>
> 1. Power Semis shows direct exposure to $NVDA 800 VDC: $NVTS (heavily relies on them for SiC), and also partners with $POWI and Lite-On.
>
> 2. Photonics exposure is through photonixFAB consortium, and three ongoing major projects in development (high-volume production in 2028). $NOK and $NVDA are active evaluators (not confirmed customers yet).
>
> There is also explicit backing through the US and European CHIPS Acts which validates their strategic importance for the West. 
>
> Their tech covers a wide spectrum of CMOS, SOI, SiC, GaN, MEMs, and MTP. They operate on 200 mm wafers and node ranging from 110nm-350nm. They don't compete with customers on IC design, assembly, test or IC sales - they are a pure-play foundry. Partnerships include $IQE, $SOI, Cadence. 
>
> Financially, it has delivered 17% CAGR over the last 5 years. Recent Q1 numbers show revenue growth was down 2%, and that the business is split into automotive (down), industrial (up 32% YoY) and medical (up). Balance sheet is quite stable with $145M in cash and $291M in net debt. 
>
> Melexis (automotive exposure customer) accounts for ~40% of their revenue. Strong baseline but also a concentration factor.
>
> Now here goes comes MY take and view. 
>
> > Technology gap compared to $TSEM: For power semis, their 200mm wafer platform is excellent for high-volume manufacturing. However, for the advanced silicon photonics cycle, tier-1 players prefer migrating toward 300mm wafers to lower optical losses and shrink component footprints. This shows X-FAB is still not the absolute best or preferred platform for the premium photonics cycle yet.
>
> > Growth upside looks heavily weighted towards photonics. Power semis will add solid revenue, but it won't be as explosive as photonics. One reason is because other IDMs like $IFX, $STM, $ON, $WOLF own their own internal fabs and don't rely on X-FAB. Shows they are not the only one in the game or as significant in town for the power semi cycle. We also don't have a lot more details on their three main ongoing photonic projects. So it is hard to be extremely bullish upfront.
>
> > 2026 is going to be a year of steady recovery, and until mid-2027 it doesn't look like the company will show significant revenue growth. Recent Q1 call also looked more bearish than bullish, and it confirmed these timelines. Plenty of time to accumulate shares for those who wish to. Would I suggest that though? Keep reading.
>
> > The downside risk is still really low because Melexis (major revenue stream) is guiding sales growth for H2'26, and with $XFAB at ~1x sales and $1B market cap, the upside is way more here. Seriously way more.
>
> Ultimately, this stock has immense potential. Would definitely be my asymmetrical pick over others that have already run so much like $TSEM, $GFS, $UMC, etc. 
>
> It looks like a 1 to 2 year long-term play, and not a quick few-months gain stock. If timelines compress, execution shows better than expected and they continue to improve on their technology sooner, we could easily see the narrative shift rapidly. This looks like something which I am optimistic on happening because that's how quick the AI infrastructure market is going forward overall. Every few months, it just surprises us.
>
> I feel $XFAB can really go 10x or even more in the next few years, but this company needs to execute really well. It still hasn't earned the "next $TSEM" tag, as they aren't worthy of it today.
>
> How would I play this?
>
> - Very worth buying a decent amount of shares here, and holding for the next 2 years. Mainly because upside is 10x+ if things fall in place.
>
> - But I wouldn't go all in at once. Rather build my position slowly and continue to accumulate over time as the story plays out.
>
> NFA. DYOR.
