### Javier Schlindwein 🐂🇦🇷 (@rjschlindwein)
_Sun Jun 14 22:44:13 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 11 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/rjschlindwein/status/2066290641995272498)

> FÁBRICAS EN EL ESPACIO
>
> $SPCX 🚀
>
> En un futuro, con costos de transporte espacial bajos, la fabricación y servicios en órbita se vuelven viables y rentables, especialmente para productos de alto valor donde la ausencia de gravedad mejora significativamente la calidad, reduce defectos por convección/sedimentación o permite estructuras imposibles en Tierra.
>
> Fabricación de Materiales Avanzados
>
> 🔸Fibras ópticas ZBLAN (o similares): En microgravedad se producen fibras con mucho menos defectos cristalinos y pérdidas de señal (hasta 10-100 veces mejores que en Tierra). Ideales para telecomunicaciones de alta velocidad, láseres médicos y sensores. Empresas como Flawless Photonics, FOMS y Made In Space ya han demostrado producción en la ISS (kilómetros de fibra).
>
> 🔸Cristales de proteínas y farmacéuticos: Crecimiento de cristales más grandes, uniformes y puros para drogas (ej. ritonavir, anticuerpos monoclonales). Mejora la formulación de medicamentos, permite nuevas terapias y acelera el descubrimiento. Varda Space ya retornó productos fabricados en órbita.
>
> 🔸Semiconductores y chips: Fabricación con menor contaminación por gravedad, mejor uniformidad en dopaje y cristales. Potencial para superar limitaciones terrestres en rendimiento y escalabilidad (apoyado por CHIPS Act).
>
> 🔸Aleaciones y materiales compuestos metálicos: Mezclas más homogéneas sin sedimentación (ej. espumas metálicas, superaleaciones). Mejores propiedades estructurales para aeronáutica, energía y herramientas.
>
> 🔸Nanomateriales y vidrios especializados: Producción de nanomateriales, vidrios exóticos o películas delgadas con propiedades únicas gracias al vacío y ausencia de convección.
>
> 🔸Impresión 3D y fabricación aditiva en órbita: Partes complejas sin soportes, estructuras grandes (vigas, paneles) optimizadas para espacio. Reduce masa lanzada y permite reparaciones in-situ o construcción de hábitats/telescopios.
>
> 🔸Bioprinting y tejidos/regenerativa: Impresión de órganos, retinas artificiales o tejidos en 3D sin colapso por gravedad. LambdaVision y otros trabajan en membranas para restaurar visión.
>
> Servicios y Otras Aplicaciones
>
> 🔹Ensamblaje y mantenimiento de grandes estructuras: Construcción de estaciones espaciales, paneles solares orbitales, telescopios gigantes o estaciones de energía solar (Space-Based Solar Power). Más fácil manejar componentes masivos sin peso.
>
> 🔹Depósitos de combustible y logística orbital: Fabricación/refinamiento de propelentes o estaciones de servicio para naves (refueling). Clave para misiones profundas.
>
> 🔹Investigación y testing de materiales: Laboratorios permanentes para probar comportamientos en microgravedad (fluidos, combustión, biología) que aceleran innovación terrestre.
>
> 🔹Producción de productos biológicos y dispositivos médicos: Cultivo de células, modelado de enfermedades o dispositivos implantables con mejor control de fluidos.
>
> 🔹Turismo y experiencias en microgravedad: fábricas orbitales podrían ofrecer tours o entornos controlados para entrenamiento/research.
>
> 🔹Reciclaje y economía circular orbital: Reprocesar desechos espaciales o satélites en nuevos materiales, reduciendo basura orbital y costos.
>
> Consideraciones Generales
>
> ☑️Ventajas clave: Ausencia de convección/burbujas/sedimentación, vacío natural, energía solar abundante y disipación de calor fácil. Ideal para productos de alto valor por kg (fibras ópticas o fármacos justifican fácilmente el transporte).
>
> ☑️Desafíos actuales: Retorno seguro a Tierra, automatización/robótica (para reducir tripulación), regulaciones (FDA para fármacos) y escalabilidad. Con costos bajos, se abre un mercado comercial masivo.
>
> ☑️Empresas pioneras: Axiom Space, Redwire/Made In Space, Varda, Flawless Photonics, Sierra Space, etc.
>
> Esta lista se basa en avances reales y proyecciones hacia 2030+. Con costos por kg cayendo drásticamente, pasará de nicho a industria transformadora, similar a cómo la reutilización revolucionó los lanzamientos.

>
> SiPh + external laser may matter more for dense, low-power optical engines.

>
> - His mindset: "trends stay trends for a long time," meaning he prefers riding established uptrends and accumulating leaders on weakness.
>
> 📚GLOSSARY
> - Pivot high:
> The most recent swing high on a chart that acts like a ceiling; breaking above it often signals more upside.
>
> - Overweight:
> A rating (here from banks) meaning they expect a stock to outperform the market and suggest owning more of it.
>
> - Consolidating:
> When a stock pauses and trades sideways after a big move, "resting" before a possible next leg.
>
> - Uptrend:
> A pattern of higher highs and higher lows showing price is generally moving up over time.
>
> - Breakout:
> When price pushes above a key resistance level, often sparking a fresh move higher.
>
> - ARR (Annual Recurring Revenue):
> The yearly revenue a company expects from ongoing/subscription contracts; a key health metric for tech firms.
>
> - Mag 7:
> Shorthand for the seven mega-cap tech leaders (e.g. Nvidia, Amazon, Alphabet, Apple) that heavily influence the market.
>
> - Watchlist:
> A list of stocks a trader monitors for a future entry rather than buying right away.

### Sh🅰️kespeare (@ShakespeareCap)
_Tue Jun 16 17:58:58 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ShakespeareCap/status/2066943630275948780)

> $NOK 
>
> Great buying point here IMO if you didn’t want to chase it at $16+. 
>
> Lots of catalysts, in a crucial spot for Physical and edge AI (AI-RAN) with all the right collaborations behind it. A lot of people have forgotten the management hinting at a big milestone during the last ER (potentially Ai-RAN related?!) later this year that could prop up the stock.  Also photonics optionality after the recent acquisition of vertically-integrated Infinera that should develop throughout the year. 
>
> Combined with the insider purchases at ATH, the glowing Nvidia investment, see no reason for the stock not to be double current price a year from now, especially as they shed portfolio/legacy segments. 
>
> If you follow me i love businesses that make ‘pivots’, by shedding legacy low-margin businesses and becoming pure plays, making valuable acquisition, turning to a new higher-demand market, etc. It tends to make the story a lot clearer for institutions, and makes the stock very easy to rerate.
>
> With all of this being said,  i am not a personal owner of $NOK, but sometimes the right way to underwrite a theme is to believe in multiple companies across the same ecosystem.
>
> My thesis is that as Physical AI develops, edge AI, lower latency, and smarter network infrastructure become dramatically more important. 
>
> Nokia is very well positioned be a dominant player here, given its NVIDIA partnership and domestic advantages. But where I see the highest upside is $HLIT (at ~2B MC vs $NOK at ~70B) as a more of an indirect beneficiary. It’s 95% monopoly over vCMTS gives it meaningful leverage if telecom, broadband, and network modernization become much more important in an AI-driven world. 
>
> Remember my earlier post: if a provider like Comcast builds out edge capabilities across its network over the next decade to support large AI workloads across millions of residential homes, I’d presume the company selling the nodes Comcast depends on to enable those edge capabilities, as well as the integrated software that dramatically improves latency, would stand to benefit.
>
> Just my musing and market thoughts. Have a great day

>
> - His method for catching big moves: on a monthly chart, find a base or trendline touch, then enter on the breakout (how he flagged $RDDT at 140).
>
> 📚GLOSSARY
> - AWAP / VWAP-style average:
> The average price a stock has traded at since listing; buyers often defend this level, making it useful support.
>
> - Horizontal support:
> A flat price floor where a stock has repeatedly stopped falling; losing it can trigger a sharp drop.
>
> - Bear trap:
> A misleading price drop that fools traders into selling or shorting right before the market reverses higher.
>
> - Relative strength:
> When a stock holds up or rises more than the overall market, a sign of leadership and demand.
>
> - VIX (rule of 16):
> The market's volatility/"fear" gauge; dividing it by 16 estimates the expected daily percentage move in the S&P 500.
>
> - 52-week high:
> The highest price a stock has hit in the past year; fresh highs often signal strong momentum.
>
> - Monthly base / breakout:
> A long sideways pause on the monthly chart, followed by a push above resistance that can start a big trend.
>
> - YTD (Year-to-Date):
> The performance of a stock counted from January 1 of the current year up to today.

### TheNewPhysics (@CharlesMullins2)
_Tue Jun 16 22:45:29 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 64 · ↻ 21 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/CharlesMullins2/status/2067015735550079297)

> 🚨 SCIENTISTS JUST ACHIEVED OPTICAL MULTISTABILITY IN A TINY MICROCAVITY  A BIG STEP FOR PHOTONIC MEMORY.
>
> In a new paper published in Nature Nanotechnology, researchers demonstrated multiple stable optical states inside a compact microcavity by using near-exceptional coupling. 
>
> This allows the device to “remember” different light intensities as distinct, stable states  something normally only possible in much larger or more complex systems.
> Optical multistability is a key requirement for multilevel optical memory and all-optical computing. Until now, achieving it in a small enough footprint for on-chip use has been extremely difficult because optical nonlinearities are usually very weak.
>
> Why this matters:
>
> • It brings us closer to practical on-chip optical memory that can store multiple bits of information per device
> • Exceptional-point physics can dramatically enhance effective nonlinearity without needing exotic materials
> • Compact multistable devices could enable faster, more energy-efficient photonic processors
> • It shows how non-Hermitian physics is becoming a powerful design tool in nanophotonics
>
> The deeper implication:
>
> We’re learning to engineer light itself to behave in increasingly complex and useful ways inside tiny structures. By operating near exceptional points, researchers can coax weak optical nonlinearities into producing strong, multistable behavior.
>
>  This kind of advance moves photonic computing from theory toward something that can actually be fabricated at scale on a chip.
>
> If this approach can be further optimized and integrated with existing silicon photonics, it could become a building block for future light-based memory and logic.
>
> How do you think compact optical multistability could accelerate the development of photonic computers?
>
> Follow for more frontier nanophotonics, exceptional-point physics, and optical computing.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/amplify_video_thumb/2067015651643060224/img/VeuCksQJj1Rvhxdb.jpg

### Marvell Technology (@MarvellTech)
_Wed Jun 17 18:09:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 109 · ↻ 20 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/MarvellTech/status/2067308699962728873)

> Contemporary silicon photonics modulators are constrained by the diffraction limit of light, restricting their ability to scale efficiently to the bandwidths AI infrastructure will require. Plasmonics offers a path forward.
>
> By compressing light below the diffraction limit at a metal-dielectric interface, plasmonic modulators can operate at speeds exceeding 1 THz, more than 10x faster than conventional photonic modulators, while measuring approximately 10 microns in length, 300x to 500x shorter. The result is exponentially higher bandwidth density within the same silicon photonics platform, without requiring a shift to new material systems.
>
> Marvell Senior Director Claudia Hoessbacher and Director Wolfgang Heni of Optical Engineering detail the technology, its applications across scale-up and scale-across networks, and where development stands today.
>
> Read more: https://t.co/3z9yPJxzac

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HLCOTnlbcAAcAhR.jpg

> Most people see $NOK as sleepy European telecom. They’re missing what it bought.
>
> Less than 2% of global semiconductor advanced test & packaging happens in the US. Nokia owns one of the only domestic sites packaging photonic chips into optical modules for AI data centers — and it didn’t come from telecom. It came from Infinera, absorbed Feb 2025.
>
> Now they’re scaling it with CHIPS money behind them:
>
> ~$30M Nokia capex + ~$10M federal CHIPS tax credit + ~$4M PA aid. 500+ jobs. Part of a $4B US commitment.
>
> This isn’t a photonics rocket — Allentown is a small piece of a $20B+ company. But that’s the point. You’re getting a CHIPS-backed domestic photonics packaging franchise inside a name the market still prices as legacy telecom.
>
> A misread legacy company with a real foothold in the AI photonics layer. The choke point before the crowd sees it.
>
> Bullish $NOK.

### dylan ツ (@demian_ai)
_Wed Jun 17 19:48:40 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 118 · ↻ 8 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/demian_ai/status/2067333627982262623)

> The best-performing thing in the AI trade this year is not the GPU, the model, or the memory
> -> it is a wafer most investors have never heard of, can't pronounce, and would struggle to explain. It ran over 1000% in one of my books. Here is what it actually is.
>
> It is the substrate. 
> The crystal wafer a laser gets grown on, sitting four layers upstream of the chip everyone watches. And the reason I trust the signal is that it did not turn up in one book. It turned up in two.
>
> I run a US bottleneck book and a separate EU one. No shared holdings, different construction, different markets. This year the strongest layer in both was the same one almost nobody can name. Not the accelerator. Not even the laser. The wafer the laser is grown on.
>
> Look at the leaderboards side by side.
>
> In the US book, InP and Substrates is the second-strongest basket of the year, behind only memory. In the EU book, InP and Substrates is also second, behind only photonics. Same layer, same rank, two markets that do not coordinate.
>
> The names tell it cleaner:
>
> - US -> $AXTI +475% YTD
> - EU -> $IQE.L +1018%, $SOI.PA (Soitec) +438%
> and $AIXA.DE (AIXTRON) +247% selling the reactors that grow the wafers
>
> The mechanism is the photonics build. Co-packaged optics needs lasers. Lasers are III-V material, indium phosphide and gallium arsenide, not plain silicon. III-V starts as an epitaxial wafer grown on a specialty substrate, and that supply is small, slow, and hard to add. When optical demand turned from slideware into orders, the squeeze hit the substrate first. Both books found the same constrained object without talking to each other.
>
> Worth the honesty: these are thin floats, so the moves are violent and part momentum. Strip the two biggest and the picture cools. But the substrate is the real upstream gate on the optics bottleneck everyone keeps drawing one layer too high.
>
> The feed watches the photonic switch. The squeeze is one floor below it, in the wafer that switch can't exist without.
>
> Dig deeper: https://t.co/93XT041lcS

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HLCkix1XwAAquIL.png

### tapebrief (@tapebrief)
_Wed Jun 17 20:12:25 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/tapebrief/status/2067339603770782182)

> Cleanest read of the quarter, and agreed it's a genuine, gimmick-free beat. The one thing I'd push on: this is a high-quality revenue print, not yet a high-quality margin one. Intelligent Infrastructure is carrying the AI growth (21%, guided +32% into Q4) but sits at 6.1% core margin, only ~30bps above the 5.8% corporate blend. So the AI surge is roughly margin-neutral to the company today. The whole re-rate toward 6%+ is a within-II mix story (photonics, cooling, power, Hanley) that management itself calls gradual. Volume is here now; the accretive mix is FY27's job. That's the gap between "beat-and-raise" and "re-rate," and it's why a 10bps full-year margin lift on a $1B revenue raise is the number to sit with.

### Joshua Fong. CFA. (@Son_JoshuaFong)
_Wed Jun 17 20:42:41 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Son_JoshuaFong/status/2067347221503471760)

> 20260617 Market Review
> • I don't to talk to you about the FOMC today. You can get that from tons of other website, talking heads etc. Most of these have no value add and not actionable. What's important is HOW do we interpret what is going and HOW do we position going forward? ie HOW DO WE THINK AHEAD OF THE CROWD?
> • Market breadth ended up being quite weak, with the VIX threatening to go back above 19 (a line in the sand I watch). But what really caught my eye was the USD. It really took off after the FOMC and stopped right at resistance. If this leads to a sustained breakout to the upside, it may not be friendly to markets. Watching that 100.50 level closely. With the USD rallying, it is no wonder $GOLD would get hit. Another lower high forming. 
> • Indices seem to be stuck in chop for now. AI seems to be the only game in town but I wanna dig deeper into the various subsectors today. 
> • Semiconductors. Ok but hitting resistance. 
> $NVDA losing the 50SMA today is not a good look. 
> • Semicon Equipment and Materials. Big list in here, very mixed picture. Nothing I would buy in a hurry.
> • Racks: $Dell ok but $HPE selling off. Neutral because the whole group is not looking uniform. 
> • Photonics: $LITE is the group leader and it has been mucking around the 50SMA. Not healthy. Neither is $AAOI, $GLW or $AXTI. 
> • Memory: $STX and $WDC still making new highs, but $MU hitting resistance. $SNDK still king. Of all the AI Hardware playes, Memory is probably the only subsector which I think overall is still healthy. But even that is extended. 
> • So the above are the AI Leading Sectors that I pay attention to and overall, my conclusion is that the easy trade in AI Hardware is over. It can still go higher, but unless it sets up for me properly (with a pullback or an orderly sideways congestion for a few weeks to a few months), I will find it hard to bet big on them for now. 
> • I am still very bullish on the AI trade but if Hardware is not the game for now, what then?
> • Next we have the Neoclouds. $IREN $CRWV $NBIS etc. $NBIS is the clear leader. Generally ok and I would still look for opportunities in them.
> • Software. I was hopeful that it might have pulled back too much and would find support but that didn't eventuate. In line with my trading philosophy, "if it ain't working, it ain't staying". I will continue to stalk this sector as they are going to be the "operational" layer of AI and I think there will be several companies in there that will benefit. 
> • Cybersecurity is one software sub-sector I am super keen on and have taken a position accordingly. Look at $CRWD and $PANW (both we took in our port today) for example. They are holding up like a champ and tightening up really nicely. This is an extremely healthy consolidation after that fierce run they had since early May, and the best part is, they are NOT giving back much of the gains! THIS is a sign of a Market Leader. Can we be wrong or too early? Of course, but then that’s why we have stops to protect us. 
> • Biotech. This is the sector that I think will benefit greatly from AI (check out the $NVDA x $LLY presentation on the NVDA website). I have been stalking XBI for a few weeks now and we finally broke higher today. Great volume too. 
> • Fintech is another interesting subsector that is showing a bit of relative strength recently. Worth keeping an eye on. Eg $DAVE $AFRM etc.
> • In conclusion, I think the overall market might be in for a bit of digestion. $MAGS  is pulling back hard (not good). The AI HARDWARE trade is no longer easy. But the AI USAGE trade I think is just starting. Biotech and Cybersecurity $CIBR are the standouts to me and we are positioning accordingly. Software $IGV is a maybe, keep stalking.
> • All the best.

### Zeek | Insights 📊 (@ZeekTyt)
_Wed Jun 17 23:44:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/ZeekTyt/status/2067393037966234024)

> $MRVL just detailed a major leap in silicon photonics for the AI era. 🔥
>
> Conventional photonic modulators are hitting the diffraction limit of light—they can’t scale fast enough for the insane bandwidth AI clusters will demand.
>
> Plasmonics changes the game. By squeezing light below the diffraction limit at a metal-dielectric interface, Marvell’s team is unlocking speeds >1 THz (10x+ faster than today’s best photonic modulators), devices only ~10 microns long (300–500x smaller), and exponentially higher bandwidth density all inside the existing silicon photonics platform.
>
> No need for exotic new materials. Just smarter physics.
>
> This directly powers the optical interconnects for next-gen scale-up and scale-across AI networks, exactly where Marvell has been building leadership (custom silicon + high-speed optics). They’ve already delivered high-speed SiPho devices with plasmonic tech in 2026, with the roadmap pointing to 3.2T+ modules and big wins in power and space efficiency.
>
> This foundational tech compounds over 5–10 years as AI infrastructure scales. Long-term holders know: connectivity is becoming as critical as the accelerators themselves.

### QSI Media - News, Analytics, World. (@MediaQSI)
_Wed Jun 17 23:49:35 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 8 · ↻ 2 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/MediaQSI/status/2067394255363170711)

> 🤖 US startup starts work on ‘first utility-scale quantum computer’ in Australia
>
> American startup PsiQuantum has begun construction on a facility in Moreton Bay, Australia, where it plans to build and deploy what it calls the world’s first utility-scale, fault-tolerant quantum computer.
>
> Unlike many quantum computing efforts that remain focused on laboratory-scale systems, PsiQuantum is pursuing a photonics-based approach designed to scale using existing semiconductor manufacturing processes and optical networking technologies.
>
> “Building a quantum computer that solves real world problems is one of the great engineering challenges of our time. For decades, quantum computing has held the promise of transforming what humanity can achieve through computation, and today in Australia we are beginning to turn that promise into reality,” — said Victor Peng, CEO of PsiQuantum.
>
> The company believes fault-tolerant quantum computers could eventually tackle problems beyond the reach of conventional computing systems. Potential applications include drug discovery, materials development, energy research, logistics, manufacturing, agriculture, and financial modeling.
>
> @MediaQSI
